 So, as far as Maven is concerned, Red5 is scope "provided".&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; You want it to reference it for compiling but should not put its classes&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; in the jar or war since you are going to sneak it into the package&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; We make a lot of aggregation jars that are used&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; in the same way.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; http://blog.artifact-software.com/tech/?p=121 describes how we handle a&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; similar need to produce skinny wars that use libraries in Tomcar/shared&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; or&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; tomcat/lib to avoid copies of the same code in multiple jars. Our LMS&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; project has over 80 Maven projects that produce a variety of jars and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; wars.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Many of these share the use of large libraries such as CXF, Spring and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Apache commons that can be shared through Tomcat's classloader rather&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; than&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; duplicated in each war.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; There are some other notes about Maven on our blog that you might find&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; interesting.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; I would prefer an installer to get the shared libraries into tomcat/lib&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; but that is another issue.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Never used "optional".&#010;What classes were missing when you used "provided"?&#010;http://maven.apache.org/guides/introduction/introduction-to-dependency-mechanism.html &#010;mentions that the transitive dependencies are not available if you use &#010;provided.&#010;You will have to add any dependencies that your code calls that are not &#010;part of Red5 but are also used by Red5.&#010;&#010;This is a good idea anyway since it documents what libraries your code &#010;actually uses.&#010;You may want to use a more recent version than the one that Red5 does.&#010;&#010;Ron&#010;&#010;&#010;On 30/04/2014 8:56 PM, Maxim Solodovnik wrote:&#010;&gt; Make the dependency "optional" seems to help :)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; On Thu, May 1, 2014 at 7:43 AM, Maxim Solodovnik &lt;solomax666@gmail.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; Thanks for your time&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I have started with making red5 "provided" but the build failed since&#010;&gt;&gt; necessary classes were not found.&#010;&gt;&gt; May be is there any way to provide dependency before build ...&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; If not I will try to create optional dependency and another one&#010;&gt;&gt; subproject, not sure if it will work.&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; I believe the blog article would be better if you can extend it a little&#010;&gt;&gt; bit and improve the formatting. Does it get eliminate the red5 classes from your jar so that it only&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; appears in the assembled war as a resource?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; To make life simpler, remove all code from the war project and put it&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; into a separate project that makes a jar that the war depends on.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; This will make it clearer when you need red5 to compile your code and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; when you need it to build a deployable war.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Maven noticing.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Pretty standard problem. Name  :- 
Rickard von Essen &lt;rickard.von.es...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
[ANN] rpm-maven-plugin 2.1-alpha-4 Released  
Date  :-
Thu, 01 May 2014 08:19:19 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the rpm-maven-plugin&#010;version 2.1-alpha-4.&#010;&#010;The RPM Maven Plugin allows artifacts from one or more projects to be&#010;packaged in an RPM for distribution. In addition to project artifacts, the&#010;RPM can contain other resources to be installed with the artifacts and&#010;scripts to be run while the package is being installed and removed. This&#010;plugin does not support the full range of features available to RPMs. In&#010;particular, source RPMs can not be generated and the spec files which are&#010;used do not do any build process (the plugin collects the files and&#010;"installs" them for packaging).&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/rpm-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin&#010;configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;        &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;        &lt;artifactId&gt;rpm-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;        &lt;version&gt;2.1-alpha-4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes:&#010;http://jira.codehaus.org/secure/ReleaseNote.jspa?projectId=11970&amp;version=19640&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;Rickard von Essen&#010;&#010;

It turns out dependency plugin is using an old version of doxia (version&#010;1.0, latest released is 1.4) that has known thread safety issues. You&#010;*might* be able to work around this by adding the following dependencies to&#010;the dependency-plugin in your pom:&#010;&#010;    &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;      &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.doxia&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;      &lt;artifactId&gt;doxia-sink-api&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;      &lt;version&gt;1.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;    &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;    &lt;dependency&gt;&#010;      &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.doxia&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;      &lt;artifactId&gt;doxia-site-renderer&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;      &lt;version&gt;1.4&lt;/version&gt;&#010;    &lt;/dependency&gt;&#010;&#010;See&#010;http://blog.sonatype.com/2008/04/how-to-override-a-plugins-dependency-in-mavenif&#010;you're unfamiliar about how to do this. this might work, but might&#010;also&#010;bug out due to some incompatibility between 1.0 and 1.4 of doxia, I did not&#010;try.&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;Please file an issue under http://jira.codehaus.org/browse/MDEP&#010;&#010;&#010;Kristian&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;2014-05-01 16:00 GMT+02:00 Anthony Clark &lt;anthonyclarka2@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi All,&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I'm trying to improve our build by using parallel threads (i.e. mvn -T #)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Unfortunately I'm running into an error when I try to use more than 9&#010;&gt; threads on this 24 core server:&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; [ERROR] Failed to execute goal&#010;&gt; org.apache.maven.plugins:maven-dependency-plugin:2.8:analyze-report&#010;&gt; (analyze-report)&#010;&gt;  on project enterprise-provided: An error has occurred in Dependency&#010;&gt; Analysis report generation. [ANN] flatten-maven-plugin 1.0.0-beta-1 Released  
Date  :-
Thu, 01 May 2014 15:55:41 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the flatten-maven-plugin version 1.0.0-beta-1.&#010;&#010;Flatten Maven Plugin generates a flattened version of your pom.xml and makes maven to install&#010;and deploy this one instead of the original pom.xml.&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/flatten-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;         &lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;         &lt;artifactId&gt;flatten-maven-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;         &lt;version&gt;1.0.0-beta-1&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;All you need to do is add the plugin to the plugins in your build section.&#010;&#010;This is the initial release.&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;  &#010;Jrg&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-
Fri, 02 May 2014 03:46:08 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache&#010;Maven Shade Plugin, version 2.3.&#010;&#010;This plugin provides the capability to package the artifact in an&#010;uber-jar, including its dependencies and to shade - i.e. rename - the&#010;packages of some of the dependencies.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-shade-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-shade-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;2.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Shade Plugin - Version 2.3&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MSHADE-166] - maven-shade-plugin not compatible with Java 8&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [MSHADE-167] - [PATCH] When individual classes are renamed, they&#010;are not debuggable&#010;&#010;&#010;Have Fun!&#010;--&#010;The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

[ANN] buildnumber-maven-plugin 1.3 Released  
Date  :-
Fri, 02 May 2014 08:28:11 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team is pleased to announce the release of the&#010;buildnumber-maven-plugin version 1.3.&#010;&#010;This mojo is designed to get a unique build number for each time you build&#010;your project. So while your version may remain constant at 1.0-SNAPSHOT for&#010;many iterations until release, you will have a build number that can&#010;uniquely identify each build during that time.&#010;&#010;http://mojo.codehaus.org/buildnumber-maven-plugin/&#010;&#010;To get this update, simply specify the version in your project's plugin&#010;configuration:&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&lt;groupId&gt;org.codehaus.mojo&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&lt;artifactId&gt; buildnumber-maven-plugin&lt; /artifactId&gt;&#010;&lt;version&gt;1.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;Release Notes&#010;https://jira.codehaus.org/secure/ReleaseNote.jspa?projectId=12124&amp;version=18855&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;The Mojo team.&#010;&#010;-- Baptiste&#010;&#010;

                                    &lt;exclude&gt;**/.git/**/*&lt;/exclude&gt;&#010;&gt;                                 &lt;/excludes&gt;&#010;&gt;                             &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;                         &lt;/execution&gt;&#010;&gt;                     &lt;/executions&gt;&#010;&gt;                 &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The pom.xml file could be found here:&#010;&gt; https://github.com/apache/incubator-stratos/blob/4.0.0-incubating/pom.xml&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Really appreciate any thoughts on this.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; Imesh Gunaratne&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; bug in maven-ear-plugin with skinny war?  
Date  :-
Mon, 05 May 2014 08:46:16 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi!&#010;&#010;I see strange behavior when using the maven EAR plugin with the&#010;skinnyWar [1] feature, which might be a bug.&#010;&#010;Here is the (simplified) module-structure I have:&#010;&#010;core&#010;  +-- core-shared&#010;&#010;web&#010;  +-- backend&#010;  +-- war&#010;&#010;ee&#010;  +-- ear&#010;&#010;Usually all modules share the same version (let's say 1.0) number. My&#010;"ear" module includes a skinny version of the war module, "core-shared"&#010;and some other 3rd-party dependencies. This works fine.&#010;&#010;However, when I update all modules to version 2.0-SNAPSHOT but keep the&#010;dependency on the "war" in the "ear" to version 1.0, the skinny war is&#010;no longer skinny. Instead the "war" 1.0 in the "ear" contains&#010;"core-shared" 1.0 dependency but the "ear" contains core-shared&#010;2.0-SNAPSHOT. Thus, the dependency is included twice with different&#010;versions.&#010;&#010;IMHO the EAR plugin doesn't respect artifact's version information&#010;when removing JARs from the skinny war, but only removes JARs that&#010;match exactly (including version string). I'd consider this a bug. Or&#010;at least a missing feature in the EAR plugin.&#010;&#010;What do others think? Should I create a JIRA entry?&#010;&#010;thx,&#010;- martin&#010;&#010;[1] http://maven.apache.org/plugins/maven-ear-plugin/examples/skinny-wars.html&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Anders Hammar &lt;and...@hammar.net&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: use separate mirrors for project dendencies and plugin dependencies ??  
Date  :-
Tue, 06 May 2014 10:53:47 GMT  
contents:- 
&gt;&#010;&gt; Presumably you are trying to separate artifacts used by plugins during&#010;&gt; your build (where you might use e.g. GPL licensed modules) from artifacts&#010;&gt; used as dependencies in your project proper (where using that same GPL&#010;&gt; licensed modules would make your legal department scream) by separating the&#010;&gt; repositories used to provide them.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; As far as I know/understand all artifacts are downloaded to the same local&#010;&gt; cache repository (~/.m2/repository), regardless of whether they were&#010;&gt; required by some plugin or as a dependency of your project.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; This makes them available for both purposes and thus obliterates all your&#010;&gt; efforts of keeping them separate.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Maven Masters: Please correct me if I'm wrong.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;I don't think this is correct with Maven 3. Maven 3 uses Aether which AFAIK&#010;keeps the repository id for the artifact to verify from where it was&#010;downloaded. Haven't verified for this use case though.&#010;&#010;So, using Maven 3 it should be possible to specify one repository&#010;declaration for your deps and one pluginRepository declaration (with a&#010;different repo id) for your plugins (incl deps). If you msut use mirror&#010;declarations, I would use this for the deps and add exclusions (using '!')&#010;for any pluginRepository.&#010;&#010;/Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Cheers,&#010;&gt; Wolf&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; On Mon, May 5, 2014 at 11:59 PM, Christian Domsch &lt;mail@landrus.de&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;  Hi Dan,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Did you consider using nexus? There you can setup any kind of strange&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; repo&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; setup your mind can come up with ;-) For your case, create one repo for&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; your project stuff and one repo for your plugin stuff. Create a group for&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; both for easy access and control access by authorization...&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Christian&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; On 06.05.2014 06:29, Dan Tran wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;  Thanks Barrie,&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Will see what I can can do.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Mon, May 5, 2014 at 5:04 PM, Barrie Treloar &lt;baerrach@gmail.com&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;   On 6 May 2014 09:21, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;   for legal purpose ( btw, please dont drill me here), I would like to&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; use&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; one mirror as a gate way for all of of my project dependencies,and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;  another&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;  mirror as a gate way for all of my plugins and their dependencies&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; is it possible? Posting a settings.xml config here is very much&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;  appreciated&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Having not done this, here is some more insane advice.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I'd use three.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; One proxy to proxy the other two proxies.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; All developers point to the master proxy.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; You can then configure the master proxy to refer to the project&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; dependencies proxy and another for plugins dependencies proxy.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; You might need a more sophisticated maven repository manager that you&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; can&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; restrict what is allowed in the proxies (i.e. it just doesn't go and&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; grab&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; stuff for you).&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; You're going to have to do a lot of fiddling to get this to work.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I'm not convinced it is going to give you what legal thinks it will...&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; If you could write up what you tried and whether it worked it would be&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; helpful for anyone else attempting the same thing...&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

On 6 May 2014 20:23, Anders Hammar &lt;anders@hammar.net&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Presumably you are trying to separate artifacts used by plugins during&#010;&gt; &gt; your build (where you might use e.g. GPL licensed modules) from artifacts&#010;&gt; &gt; used as dependencies in your project proper (where using that same GPL&#010;&gt; &gt; licensed modules would make your legal department scream) by separating&#010;&gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; repositories used to provide them.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; As far as I know/understand all artifacts are downloaded to the same&#010;&gt; local&#010;&gt; &gt; cache repository (~/.m2/repository), regardless of whether they were&#010;&gt; &gt; required by some plugin or as a dependency of your project.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; This makes them available for both purposes and thus obliterates all your&#010;&gt; &gt; efforts of keeping them separate.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; Maven Masters: Please correct me if I'm wrong.&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I don't think this is correct with Maven 3. Maven 3 uses Aether which AFAIK&#010;&gt; keeps the repository id for the artifact to verify from where it was&#010;&gt; downloaded. Haven't verified for this use case though.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; So, using Maven 3 it should be possible to specify one repository&#010;&gt; declaration for your deps and one pluginRepository declaration (with a&#010;&gt; different repo id) for your plugins (incl deps). If you msut use mirror&#010;&gt; declarations, I would use this for the deps and add exclusions (using '!')&#010;&gt; for any pluginRepository.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; /Anders&#010;&#010;&#010;I don't remember what happens for duplicates.&#010;I think it used to complain that the artifact doesn't exist (if the one it&#010;downloaded from is not available, even though its available elsewhere).&#010;&#010;The GPL example isn't a good one, as the output of running GPL is not GPL&#010;itself.&#010;&#010;I think Nexus allows you to restrict things by licence so that you can&#010;curate what is available in your repository manager. You'd have to look at&#010;the docs to find out.&#010;&#010;

&gt; &gt; your build (where you might use e.g. GPL licensed modules) from&#010;&gt; artifacts&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; used as dependencies in your project proper (where using that same GPL&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; licensed modules would make your legal department scream) by separating&#010;&gt; &gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; repositories used to provide them.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; As far as I know/understand all artifacts are downloaded to the same&#010;&gt; &gt; local&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; cache repository (~/.m2/repository), regardless of whether they were&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; required by some plugin or as a dependency of your project.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; You'd have to look at&#010;&gt; the docs to find out.&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

wrote:&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Presumably you are trying to separate artifacts used by plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; during&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; your build (where you might use e.g. GPL licensed modules) from&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; artifacts&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; used as dependencies in your project proper (where using that&#010;&gt; same&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; GPL&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; licensed modules would make your legal department scream) by&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; separating&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; repositories used to provide them.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; As far as I know/understand all artifacts are downloaded to&#010;the&#010;&gt; &gt; same&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; local&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; cache repository (~/.m2/repository), regardless of whether they&#010;&gt; &gt; were&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; required by some plugin or as a dependency of your project.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; This makes them available for both purposes and thus obliterates&#010;&gt; &gt; all&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; your&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; efforts of keeping them separate.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Maven Masters: Please correct me if I'm wrong.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I don't think this is correct with Maven 3. Maven 3 uses Aether&#010;&gt; which&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; AFAIK&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; keeps the repository id for the artifact to verify from where it&#010;&gt; was&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; downloaded. Haven't verified for this use case though.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; So, using Maven 3 it should be possible to specify one repository&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; declaration for your deps and one pluginRepository declaration&#010;&gt; (with&#010;&gt; &gt; a&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; different repo id) for your plugins (incl deps). If you msut use&#010;&gt; &gt; mirror&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; declarations, I would use this for the deps and add exclusions&#010;&gt; (using&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; '!')&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; for any pluginRepository.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; /Anders&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I don't remember what happens for duplicates.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I think it used to complain that the artifact doesn't exist (if the&#010;&gt; one&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; it&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; downloaded from is not available, even though its available&#010;&gt; elsewhere).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; The GPL example isn't a good one, as the output of running GPL is not&#010;&gt; &gt; GPL&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; itself.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I think Nexus allows you to restrict things by licence so that you&#010;&gt; can&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; curate what is available in your repository manager. You'd have to&#010;&gt; look&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; at&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; the docs to find out.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Maven 3 uses Aether&#010;&gt; &gt; which&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; AFAIK&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; keeps the repository id for the artifact to verify from where&#010;it&#010;&gt; &gt; was&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; downloaded. Haven't verified for this use case though.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; So, using Maven 3 it should be possible to specify one repository&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; declaration for your deps and one pluginRepository declaration&#010;&gt; &gt; (with&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; a&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; different repo id) for your plugins (incl deps). If you msut&#010;use&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; mirror&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; declarations, I would use this for the deps and add exclusions&#010;&gt; &gt; (using&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; '!')&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; for any pluginRepository.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; /Anders&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I don't remember what happens for duplicates.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I think it used to complain that the artifact doesn't exist (if the&#010;&gt; &gt; one&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; it&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; downloaded from is not available, even though its available&#010;&gt; &gt; elsewhere).&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; The GPL example isn't a good one, as the output of running GPL is&#010;&gt; not&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; GPL&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; itself.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I think Nexus allows you to restrict things by licence so that you&#010;&gt; &gt; can&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; curate what is available in your repository manager. You'd have to&#010;&gt; &gt; look&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; at&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; the docs to find out.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Presumably you are trying to separate artifacts used&#010;by&#010;&gt; plugins&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; during&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; your build (where you might use e.g. GPL licensed&#010;modules)&#010;&gt; from&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; artifacts&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; As far as I know/understand all artifacts are downloaded&#010;to&#010;&gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; same&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; local&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; cache repository (~/.m2/repository), regardless of&#010;whether&#010;&gt; they&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; were&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; required by some plugin or as a dependency of your&#010;project.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; This makes them available for both purposes and thus&#010;&gt; &gt; obliterates&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; all&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; your&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; efforts of keeping them separate.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; Maven Masters: Please correct me if I'm wrong.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I don't think this is correct with Maven 3. Subject  :-
[ANN] Apache Maven Plugin Tools (including Maven Plugin Plugin) 3.3 Released  
Date  :-
Thu, 08 May 2014 13:30:29 GMT  
contents:- 
The Apache Maven team is pleased to announce the release of the Apache Maven &#010;Plugin Tools, version 3.3&#010;&#010;The Maven Plugin Tools contains the necessary tools to be able to produce &#010;Maven Plugins in scripting languages and to generate rebarbative content like &#010;descriptor, help and documentation.&#010;&#010;The Maven Plugin Plugin is used to create a Maven plugin descriptor for any &#010;Mojo's found in the source tree, to include in the JAR. It is also used to &#010;generate report files for the Mojos as well as for updating the plugin &#010;registry, the artifact metadata and generating a generic help goal.&#010;&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugin-tools/&#010;http://maven.apache.org/plugin-tools/maven-plugin-plugin/&#010;&#010;You should specify the version in your project's plugin configuration:&#010;&#010;&lt;plugin&gt;&#010;  &lt;groupId&gt;org.apache.maven.plugins&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;  &lt;artifactId&gt;maven-plugin-plugin&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;  &lt;version&gt;3.3&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&#010;&#010;Release Notes - Maven Plugin Tools - Version 3.3&#010;&#010;** Bug&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-191] - plugin-info.html is not created&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-234] - Extreme amounts of debug logging&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-235] - Doc example incorrectly states that plexus-utils is &#010;needed as a dependency&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-236] - Value for Mojo's 'defaultPhase' parameter is incorrectly &#010;a string in examples&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-239] - Execute goal does not passes from mojos.xml &#010;pluginMetadata&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-242] - NullPointerException in MojoClassVisitor.visit()&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-244] - Help mojo generates Javadoc, which is not accepted by &#010;JDK 8 doclint&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-245] - @Parameter property names are not written to the plugin-&#010;help.xml file&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-248] - XML-Namespace in ITs for ant-based mojos are wrong.&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-255] - Generated HelpMojo doesn't close resource stream&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-258] - IT failures with Jdk 8 (EA) &#010;    * [MPLUGIN-260] - Plugin that uses annotations in Java 8 source can't &#010;generate descriptor&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-262] - Generated HelpMojo doesn't display default values and &#010;user properties.&#010;&#010;** Improvement&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-237] - JavaDoc WARNING on generated HelpMojo class.&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-246] - Clarify that super class must also use annotations&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-264] - Allow other packaging types&#010;&#010;** New Feature&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-259] - @Parameter name="xxx" to set bean property name different &#010;from class' field&#010;&#010;** Task&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-233] - remove InstanciationStrategy enum from annotations&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-265] - remove deprecated API since introduction of &#010;PluginToolsRequest&#010;&#010;** Wish&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-249] - give snippets to show use of expressions to get Maven &#010;objects&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-250] - since element is not in version 1.0.0 of plugin-&#010;metadata: should create a new version of the descriptor&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-257] - deprecate classical Maven objects as components&#010;    * [MPLUGIN-261] - sort goals in generated plugin.xml&#010;&#010;Enjoy,&#010;&#010;-The Apache Maven team&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010; How to override settings for maven module  
Date  :-
Fri, 09 May 2014 00:59:31 GMT  
contents:- 
I have a master POM file which defines common stuff such as common &#010;dependencies like junit and compiler settings.&#010;&#010;The compiler settings are set to treat warning as error using &#010;maven-compiler-plugin and Werror as compiler argument. I have a new &#010;module which declares the master pom as parent pom, but has generated &#010;code which has lot of warnings. I would like to disable treating &#010;warnings as errors only for this module or if possible only for &#010;generated package or generated source directory.&#010;&#010;I tried adding compiler plugin entry in module's pom file. But it looks &#010;like it overrides from parent. How do I disable warnings for this module &#010;only?&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;&#010;Niranjan&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Niranjan Rao &lt;nhr...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How to override settings for maven module  
Date  :-
Fri, 09 May 2014 17:36:15 GMT  
contents:- 
Found the answer, you need to use combine.self="override" in the &#010;compiler plugin settings. More details at &#010;http://stackoverflow.com/questions/1771561/maven-is-it-possible-to-override-the-configuration-of-a-plugin-already-defined&#010;&#010;On 05/08/2014 05:59 PM, Niranjan Rao wrote:&#010;&gt; I have a master POM file which defines common stuff such as common &#010;&gt; dependencies like junit and compiler settings.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The compiler settings are set to treat warning as error using &#010;&gt; maven-compiler-plugin and Werror as compiler argument. Karl Heinz Marbaise &lt;khmarba...@gmx.de&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: How to override settings for maven module  
Date  :-
Mon, 12 May 2014 16:31:30 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;the first thing in such situations is to create a separate module which &#010;contains the generation code part. In this module you can change the &#010;configuration for maven-compiler-plugin via a pluginManagemen block...&#010;&#010;So looks like this:&#010;&#010;   parent (pom.xml)&#010;     +-- mod-generated (pom.xml)&#010;     +-- mod-the-rest (pom.xml)&#010;&#010;If you follow this suggestions you have clear separation of concern for &#010;your modules and you only need to change the configuration for the &#010;mod-generated.&#010;&#010;Kind regards&#010;Karl-Heinz Marbaise&#010;&#010;On 5/9/14 2:59 AM, Niranjan Rao wrote:&#010;&gt; I have a master POM file which defines common stuff such as common&#010;&gt; dependencies like junit and compiler settings.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; The compiler settings are set to treat warning as error using&#010;&gt; maven-compiler-plugin and Werror as compiler argument. I would like to disable treating&#010;&gt; warnings as errors only for this module or if possible only for&#010;&gt; generated package or generated source directory.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; I tried adding compiler plugin entry in module's pom file. M2Eclipse vs. maven-eclipse-plugin: which is preferred?  
Date  :-
Fri, 09 May 2014 09:19:50 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi all,&#010;&#010;Does the Apache Maven Project/Community has an official stance about&#010;whether M2Eclipse or maven-eclipse-plugin is preferred way of importing&#010;Maven projects into Eclipse?&#010;&#010;I thought M2Eclipse was the blessed way, but I cannot find anything&#010;"official" online.&#010;Only that the maven-eclipse-plugin hasn't been updated for a while, but&#010;that could also be a sign that it has no issue and Eclipse offers backwards&#010;compatibility.&#010;&#010;Note: this is not a poll about what you as a developer prefers, I'm looking&#010;for whether there's an official position and which one it is.&#010;Background: I'm in a argument in a code review for an archetype about&#010;whether to include maven-eclipse-plugin configuration within the POM or&#010;not; and any "official" choice would help us avoid "bikeshedding".&#010;&#010;&#010;-- &#010;Thomas Broyer&#010;/t.ma.bwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Jason van Zyl &lt;ja...@takari.io&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: M2Eclipse vs. maven-eclipse-plugin: which is preferred?  
Date  :-
Thu, 15 May 2014 17:58:34 GMT  
contents:- 
There is nothing official from the Maven itself. There used to be competing Maven Eclipse integration&#010;from different people here, and there has always been the command line generation vs IDE integration.&#010;So there is no officially blessed integration from the Maven project proper.&#010;&#010;Also note that M2Eclipse and the maven-eclipse-plugin are not compatible. In M2E it specifically&#010;looks for project files created with the maven-eclipse-plugin and disables them.&#010;&#010;On May 9, 2014, at 2:19 AM, Thomas Broyer &lt;t.broyer@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi all,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Does the Apache Maven Project/Community has an official stance about&#010;&gt; whether M2Eclipse or maven-eclipse-plugin is preferred way of importing&#010;&gt; Maven projects into Eclipse?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I thought M2Eclipse was the blessed way, but I cannot find anything&#010;&gt; "official" online.&#010;&gt; Only that the maven-eclipse-plugin hasn't been updated for a while, but&#010;&gt; that could also be a sign that it has no issue and Eclipse offers backwards&#010;&gt; compatibility.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Note: this is not a poll about what you as a developer prefers, I'm looking&#010;&gt; for whether there's an official position and which one it is.&#010;&gt; Background: I'm in a argument in a code review for an archetype about&#010;&gt; whether to include maven-eclipse-plugin configuration within the POM or&#010;&gt; not; and any "official" choice would help us avoid "bikeshedding".&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; -- &#010;&gt; Thomas Broyer&#010;&gt; /t.ma.bwa.je/ &lt;http://xn--nna.ma.xn--bwa-xxb.je/&gt;&#010;&#010;Thanks,&#010;&#010;Jason&#010;&#010;----------------------------------------------------------&#010;Jason van Zyl&#010;Founder,  Apache Maven&#010;http://twitter.com/jvanzyl&#010;http://twitter.com/takari_io&#010;---------------------------------------------------------&#010;&#010;We all have problems. How we deal with them is a measure of our worth.&#010;&#010; -- Unknown&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-

contents:- 
Hi,&#010;&#010;I want to execute a project-less maven plugin from the command line.&#010;However the plugin is not in maven central and I cannot place the plugin&#010;repository in the settings.xml file.&#010;&#010;Now I can use the dependency:get plugin to fetch the plugin from the&#010;remote repository into my local repository. However I have to use the&#010;command line switch -llr, which triggers a warning. Otherwise maven&#010;complains about the fact that the plugin cannot be found at maven&#010;central (though it really is in the local repository).&#010;&#010;Adding -llr works, and the plugin is found.&#010;&#010;However I would like to have a way were I can run a project-less plugin,&#010;from the command line, using an alternate plugin repository.&#010;&#010;Like:&#010;    mvn mygroup:myartifact:1.2.3:do-my-stuff&#010;-Dmaven.plugin.repository=http://my.own/repository&#010;&#010;I have not found such a property in the documentation.&#010;&#010;Jens&#010;&#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Bernd Eckenfels &lt;e...@zusammenkunft.net&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Sharing of values across dependant projects?  
Date  :-
Thu, 15 May 2014 10:01:05 GMT  
contents:- 
Is A released after each built-number change or is it a snapshot? In the snapshot case you&#010;can add a snapshot dependency and then see the number in the classpath. Maven will find the&#010;latest updates. If you make a release I guess it is easier to use a built parameter passed&#010;by Jenkins to both projects in a Pipeline. (Or to actually commit changes to version control,&#010;hard to say without details).&#010;&#010;You could also use the versions-plugin to programmatically bump the dependency version in&#010;project B and then run a second maven invocation to build it.&#010;&#010;Gruss&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;&gt; Am 09.05.2014 um 16:02 schrieb James Green &lt;james.mk.green@gmail.com&gt;:&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; I have two projects - A and B. Name  :- 
Curtis Rueden &lt;ctrue...@wisc.edu&gt;  
Subject  :-
Re: Sharing of values across dependant projects?  
Date  :-
Fri, 16 May 2014 20:23:55 GMT  
contents:- 
Hi James,&#010;&#010;&gt; I have two projects - A and B. B depends on A.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A is built with a number (call it a build number). B needs to which number&#010;&gt; is in A at the time B builds.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Any ideas how to achieve this without any human intervention?&#010;&#010;For B to query A at *runtime* of B: embed your build numbers in the JAR&#010;manifest.&#010;&#010;With the buildnumber-maven-plugin, it's something like this:&#010;https://github.com/scijava/pom-scijava/blob/69b3520e486b2a3d65636833efe230b00f3ea78f/pom.xml#L680&#010;And this:&#010;https://github.com/scijava/pom-scijava/blob/69b3520e486b2a3d65636833efe230b00f3ea78f/pom.xml#L567&#010;&#010;Then you can extract the version information out the manifest using Java's&#010;built-in API:&#010;http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/util/jar/JarFile.html#getManifest()&#010;http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/index.html?java/util/jar/Manifest.html&#010;&#010;To query A at B's *build* time as you request -- i.e., for your Jenkins job&#010;that builds B to query the version of A, to decide whether to even build --&#010;you could use the Jenkins Groovy plugin with the "Poll with a Groovy&#010;script" ScriptTrigger that checks whether the build number changed since&#010;the last build, using the above approach...&#010;&#010;But is there some reason it's not good enough to simply have B's build be a&#010;downstream job of A's build?&#010;&#010;Regards,&#010;Curtis&#010;&#010;&#010;On Fri, May 9, 2014 at 9:02 AM, James Green &lt;james.mk.green@gmail.com&gt;wrote:&#010;&#010;&gt; I have two projects - A and B. B depends on A.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; A is built with a number (call it a build number). B needs to which number&#010;&gt; is in A at the time B builds.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; Any ideas how to achieve this without any human intervention?&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; FWIW the use case here is that A is software distributed by B (a WAR&#010;&gt; archive). A queries B for an updated build number, thus implementing&#010;&gt; "automatic updates". I'm trying to automate the setting of this number&#010;&gt; across the two projects but I've drawn a blank inside Jenkins for the&#010;&gt; moment.&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; James&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

Name  :- 
Nick Dimiduk &lt;ndimi...@gmail.com&gt;  
Subject  :-
Shading all modules in a project  
Date  :-
Mon, 12 May 2014 16:01:31 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;Over in Apache HBase, we have an interesting problem that I'm hoping the&#010;shade plugin can help us solve. It all started with a performance&#010;enhancement to reduce garbage by creating a subclass of a protobuf type&#010;[0]. It works fine for us most of the time. However, when using this code&#010;from a Hadoop mapreduce job, things get strange. Due to the permissions on&#010;the parent object and the way Hadoop uses "fat" jars, we now have&#010;classloader troubles [1]. We were able to work around the issue by&#010;documenting the required classpath constructions. However, this is not&#010;possible for all users. This is where the shade plugin comes in.&#010;&#010;I gave shade a shot [2], though I admit I'm not terribly familiar with it,&#010;nor the inner workings of maven. As far as I can tell, the trouble is the&#010;plugin invocation is limited to the single module in our multi-module&#010;project. I think what's happening is shade is doing what I want for the&#010;hbase-protocol module, but I also need it to do bytecode rewriting for the&#010;modules that consume this module as well. Luckily, this detail is not part&#010;of our public API so it should be transparent to our users.&#010;&#010;My patch is posted on [2]. Any pointers/advice is greatly appreciated.&#010;&#010;Thanks in advance,&#010;Nick&#010;&#010;[0]: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/HBASE-9867&#010;[1]: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/HBASE-10304&#010;[2]: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/HBASE-11118&#010;&#010;

It all started with a performance&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; enhancement to reduce garbage by creating a subclass of a protobuf type&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; [0]. It works fine for us most of the time. However, when using this&#010;&gt; code&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; from a Hadoop mapreduce job, things get strange. Due to the&#010;&gt; permissions on&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; the parent object and the way Hadoop uses "fat" jars&#010;&gt; MG&gt;Uberjar or KitchenSinkJar or FatJar or SealedJar forces the situation of&#010;&gt; MG&gt;whenever any of the dependencies in fatjar change that you are packing&#010;&gt; into fatjar you will need to trigger a repackage of FatJar&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;we now have&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; classloader troubles [1]. We were able to work around the issue by&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; documenting the required classpath constructions. However, this is not&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; possible for all users. This is where the shade plugin comes in.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; I gave shade a shot [2], though I admit I'm not terribly familiar with&#010;&gt; it,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; nor the inner workings of maven. As far as I can tell, the trouble is&#010;&gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; plugin invocation is limited to the single module in our multi-module&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; project. I think what's happening is shade is doing what I want for the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; hbase-protocol module&#010;&gt; MG&gt;yes but every time the original (non-shaded) project you are shading is&#010;&gt; updated&#010;&gt; MG&gt;then you will need a mechanism to trigger that update to your shaded&#010;&gt; jar (to grab those deltas)&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;but I also need it to do bytecode rewriting&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;for the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; modules that consume this module as well. Luckily, this detail is not&#010;&gt; part&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; of our public API so it should be transparent to our users.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; My patch is posted on [2]. Any pointers/advice is greatly appreciated.&#010;&gt; MG&gt;break the fat jars into discrete individual maven artifacts is what i&#010;&gt; would suggest&#010;&gt; MG&gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Thanks in advance,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; Nick&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; [0]: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/HBASE-9867&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; [1]: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/HBASE-10304&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; [2]: https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/HBASE-11118&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt;&#010;&#010;

We were able to work around the issue by&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; documenting the required classpath constructions. However, this is&#010;&gt; not&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; possible for all users. This is where the shade plugin comes in.&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; I gave shade a shot [2], though I admit I'm not terribly familiar&#010;&gt; with&#010;&gt; &gt; it,&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; nor the inner workings of maven. As far as I can tell, the trouble is&#010;&gt; &gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; plugin invocation is limited to the single module in our multi-module&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; project. I think what's happening is shade is doing what I want for&#010;&gt; the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; hbase-protocol module&#010;&gt; &gt; MG&gt;yes but every time the original (non-shaded) project you are shading&#010;&gt; is&#010;&gt; &gt; updated&#010;&gt; &gt; MG&gt;then you will need a mechanism to trigger that update to your shaded&#010;&gt; &gt; jar (to grab those deltas)&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt;&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;but I also need it to do bytecode rewriting&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt;for the&#010;&gt; &gt; &gt; &gt; modules that consume this module as well. Subject  :-
Re: Version in Mojo  
Date  :-
Thu, 15 May 2014 17:43:11 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello,&#010;&#010;this is not really Mojo specific.&#010;&#010;If you build a JAR with maven you can&#010;include the build number or version with filtered resources, filtering&#010;the source code, as a expanded Variable in the Manifest header or by&#010;copy of META-INF/maven/pom.properties. To any of those information you&#010;can then reference to print it out.&#010;&#010;This is an example I use (you need to use a class of your project and&#010;add maven group and artifactID):&#010;&#010;    /** Read program version from Manifest or maven properties. */&#010;    private static String getVersion()&#010;    {&#010;        Class me = MyClass.class;&#010;        Package jarPackage = me.getPackage();&#010;        if (jarPackage != null)&#010;        {&#010;            String version = jarPackage.getImplementationVersion();&#010;            if (version != null)&#010;            {&#010;                return version;&#010;            }&#010;        }&#010;        InputStream in =&#010;        me.getClassLoader().getResourceAsStream("META-INF/maven/groupID/artifactID/pom.properties");&#010;        if (in == null) { return "UNKNOWN";}&#010;        try&#010;        {&#010;            Properties p = new Properties();&#010;            p.load(in);&#010;            return p.getProperty("version", "UNKNOWN");&#010;        }&#010;        catch (Exception ignored)&#010;        {&#010;            return "UNKNOWN";&#010;        }&#010;        finally&#010;        {&#010;            try { in.close(); } catch (Exception ignored) { /* ignored&#010;    */ } }&#010;    }&#010;&#010;Greetings&#010;Bernd&#010;&#010;&#010; Am Wed, 14 May 2014 07:41:27 -0700&#010;(PDT) schrieb DenisDasKind &lt;bltomov@abv.bg&gt;:&#010;&#010;&gt; Hi,&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; i'm new to maven, and now i have the following problem. I have a&#010;&gt; custom Mojo, and the Mojo should print the own version stored in the&#010;&gt; pom.xml of this mojo. And now i have trouble to get this version. I&#010;&gt; have tried the project.version, but this is always the version of the&#010;&gt; pom, that calls my Mojo. A easy way, will be when the version is&#010;&gt; hardcoded, but this is not the best way, becausae each time when the&#010;&gt; version is changed (release) i must change it manually.&#010;&gt; Is there a better way to get this version?&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; Thank you in advance!&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; --&#010;&gt; View this message in context:&#010;&gt; http://maven.40175.n5.nabble.com/Version-in-Mojo-tp5793054.html Sent&#010;&gt; from the Maven - Users mailing list archive at Nabble.com.&#010;&gt; &#010;&gt; ---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;&gt; To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&gt; &#010;&#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

It has no influence on the Maven build itself. --&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;            &lt;plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;              &lt;groupId&gt;org.eclipse.m2e&lt;/groupId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;              &lt;artifactId&gt;lifecycle-mapping&lt;/artifactId&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;              &lt;version&gt;1.0.0&lt;/version&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;              &lt;configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;                ...&#010;&gt;&gt;              &lt;/configuration&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;            &lt;/plugin&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;          &lt;/plugins&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;        &lt;/pluginManagement&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;      &lt;/build&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt;    &lt;/profile&gt;&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; Beautiful, right? ;-)&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; -Curtis&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; On Fri, May 16, 2014 at 2:48 PM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; any one?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; http://central.maven.org/maven2/org/eclipse/m2e&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; -D&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; On Thu, May 15, 2014 at 4:34 PM, Dan Tran &lt;dantran@gmail.com&gt; wrote:&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; I am looking for org.eclipse.m2e:lifecycle-mapping:1.0.0&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; and it is not at maven central any more.&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; do you see the same thing?&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; Thanks&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; -D&#010;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt;&gt; &#010;&gt;&gt; &#010;&#010;---------------------------------------------------------------------&#010;To unsubscribe, e-mail: users-unsubscribe@maven.apache.org&#010;For additional commands, e-mail: users-help@maven.apache.org&#010;&#010;&#010;

Date  :-
Fri, 16 May 2014 15:17:48 GMT  
contents:- 
Hello, &#010;&#010;i am trying to transfert documentation for an application, which is written using a .odt file,&#010;to some doxia process, so i can be sure pdf is the lastest version in the build. &#010;&#010;However, i am facing a surprisingly basic problem: i can't find out how to include an inline&#010;image. That is, i can put image before, or after a paragraph, but i can't put it inside a&#010;paragraph. I tried xhtml, apt, confluence, twiki, xdoc and markdown. &#010;&#010;Here are my results: &#010;apt -&gt; there is no way to make an inline image in apt &#010;confluence -&gt; while the language allows it, and the eclipse confluence parser shows it&#010;properly, the image tag is not read by doxia and the wiki code appear as is on the final document.&#010;image is properly recognized when inside a paragraph &#010;twiki -&gt; didn't find a way to make an inline image &#010;markdown -&gt; image tag is recognized inline, but everything after the tag, in same paragraph,&#010;is ignored. &#010;xhtml -&gt; while verbose, this language does allow inline image. Unfortunately, all inline&#010;image are showed above paragraph in the resulting pdf, not inline. &#010;xdoc -&gt; the parser just doesn't kick in, doxia think it's a docbook and messes everything&#010;&#010;&#010;So, my question is simple: how can i put an inline image in a doxia document. Which markup&#010;language must i use, and what is the process? &#010;&#010;Best result i got so far was with xhtml, and it looked like this in pdf, &#010;http://i.imgur.com/82mL281.png &#010;&#010;when it should have looked about like this (original open office document): &#010;http://i.imgur.com/UEDuQf1.png &#010;&#010;&#010;David Delbecq &#010;&#010;&#010;
